<Author>araf
<Content>Let's not get carried away here Stayed here last week. Location great and hotel ambience super.Young staff very attentive and well trained.Our biggest gripe as mentioned by others was the noise in the rooms coming from the central atrium at the bottom of which was the bar area.Rooms have wooden floors anyway so beware the clip clop of heels above or to the side of your room. In all these hotels that have rooms around a central atrium they need another door to insulate the noise in the hall area before the bedroom area and this hotel does not have these. In our case in room 210 near the lifts we could hear most comings and goings all night at the lifts and needless to say with the regular supply of inconsiderate guests who speak at full volume at even 4.00am we had basically three nights with interrupted sleep. On this basis I couldn't recommend the hotel to others.View from room 210 not great either other than great roof sculptures of the CA building of all places!The breakfasts were so so with erratic service from day to day. One day with coffee top ups every few minutes to the following day when we had to go find it ourselves. Hot selections were also not kept hot for long as there was no heating system resulting in tepid bacon and burgers!! and scarmbled egg. The buffet breakfast at the next door sister Hotel Regina looked much better.We stayed on a romantic break package which packaged the breakfast s with a bottle of Cava which we drank in the bar on a Wednesday night when they have live music (finishes 10pm). Most of the other people in the bar on all three nights were local young vistors not staying at the hotel. Coffee price in bar E3.00.Had a bar meal on night two which was of good quality at Burger E10.50 with Artisan chips for E5.50.Other tips for your stay.Caught train RENFE from airport E2.60 each -change at Barcelona Sants still on RENFE to Pl de Catalunya. The road for the Pulitzer is off the Plaza directly opposite the Corte Ingles apartment store.Meals ; had a great al fresco meal at El Cafe d'en Victor which is near the Cathedral in the Gothic quarter. Menu del dia for E12.00 sit outside price -three courses and a carafe of wine with Sea Bass as main course.Decent meal also at Siddartha on Carrer d'AvenyoTry and go for the day to Sitges. We went by train at E5.20 return each, takes about 30 mins and it is a lovely place to sit in the sun and eat if you can at the Costa Dorada just below the church by the beach where you can while away the day with beer and tapas. Heaven.Back to Barcelona. Go by cable car up to Montjuic and walk down to savour the great views.Great city full of shops for young people.

<Author>JCWLondon
<Content>Absolutely fantastic hotel - would recommend We have just come back from a 4 day stay at Hotel Pulitzer.I had emailed the hotel Manager as it was a special trip for my boyfriend celebrating his birthday. Upon arrival at the hotel by taxi from the airport (about 25-30 euro) we had an easy check in with a very helpful member of reception staff. He informed us that they had upgraded our room which was a really nice surprise.The room wasn't ready at 2pm check in time but we didn't mind as it gave us the opportunity to check the bar and have a little wonder around the hotel.The room, once we checked in was lovely. Had a lovely comfy bed, tv on the wall, safe, sofa, large wardrobe, mini bar and then a lovely modern bathroom with large bath, and a granite sink. His and Hers ammenity kits along with a kit for Both as well!Also another lovely surprise was a bottle of champagne and a chocolate birthday cake for my boyfriend. I had forgotten a travel adaptor and the hotel reception were able to provide this.We had dinner in the hotel the first night which was really nice. It was extremely quiet but then eating at 9pm in Spain is very early! Service was very good and the food delicious.The reception staff couldn't have been more helpful during our stay with any enquiries we had.The roof terrace was closed as it is winter but looks really lovely. We managed to take our drinks up there whilst we were waiting for our room - a real sun trap!The location is perfect at the top of La Rambla and a great starting point to almost anywhere! A taxi rank is very close by.One thing to mention about the complimentary use of the Holmes Place. It is a good 5-10 minute walk away and if you plan to use the swimming pool and jacuzzi you need a swimming hat and flip flops to use around the pool area. This meant we couldn't swim or use the lovely looking jacuzzi which was a shame. We did manage to use the steam and sauna which were really nice but pack a swimming hat if you intend on using these facilities!! (Maybe get away with the hotel slippers if you don't have flip flops!)Check out was easy and the staff kept our cases until we needed to leave. They booked us a car to the airport which was on time and the driver very pleasant which was a nice end to a fab holiday.I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone and would thank all staff at the Hotel Pulitzer for making our stay so enjoyable.

<Author>Silverpink25
<Content>Flawless Stay at Hotel Pulitzer My husband and I just got back from our 10-day honeymoon in Europe, during which we stayed in 3 different hotels, and Hotel Pulitzer was hands-down our favorite. In fact, I'm going to go there and say that it was the best hotel I've ever stayed in. HP was the first hotel of our trip and it could not have started any better.The service, the decor, and the location were all superb. The rooms were small, yes, but sleek and modern and completely comfortable for two people who were mostly in and out. We had a room overlooking the street (which I'd recommend) with those classic Barcelona-style doors that open to a small balcony. The views were fantastic. The bathroom was also modern and sleek, with a dark granite decor. The bed had lots of pillows and was very comfortable!Another thing we really loved was the bar. The bartenders were true professionals and made the most well-executed cocktails I have ever seen! I greatly recommend trying some of the drinks on their menu because all that we tried were amazing. They really take their time and use great quality ingredients (try the mojito and the white russian!). They were also friendly and helpful. They recommended a tapas restaurant to us (Origens), that ended up being the best dining experience of our trip. The space is also cool. You can sit at the bar or settle in at one of the many comfy spots throughout the lounge. On most nights, there were small groups of people congregating throughout. There is also a really cute little back garden. One night while we were there, they had some live jazz, which just added to the experience even more!In addition to the service at the bar, the overall hotel service was also excellent. Never having been to Barcelona before, we had many questions and requests and they were always incredibly accomodating and friendly. Finally, the location was great, especially for someone just getting the know the city. It's a block of so from La Rambla, which is a great starting point for any direction you want to go in. Needless to say, we were very sad when it came time to check out of Hotel Pulitzer. If I ever find myself in Barcelona again, I will be returning!

<Author>Jaatinen
<Content>Average hotel at great location We chose this hotel on the basis of the location and the reviews in TripAdvisor.The location is excellent. In the middle of everything, very close to La Rambla and Placa Catalunya. Spot on.Otherwise there was nothing special in this hotel.The hotel was art deco style - we have nothing against it, but there was nothing special in the interior that would have warmed our hearts.The room was OK, but again nothing that would make me long for this hotel.The bed was average and OK, but with these room prices I would have assumed a higher level of quality. Still OK.What was not at all OK was the soundproofing of the rooms.The exerior walls and the windows let all the street noise in - including louder conversations of passer-bys.Also the in house noise of the bar (clings and clangs of the glasses) three levels down continued late and was clearly audible inside the room. Fortunately we were so exhausted of walking the lovely streets of Barcelona that we fell instantly asleep. But if you have any trouble with your sleep think what I just wrote above.Breakfast was OK.The staff was OK as well, but again there was nothing that would make me say they were particularly friendly. Summa summarum: excellent location - bad soundproofing - everything else average.

<Author>Phillyfans
<Content>Perfect Location, Great Staff and Excellent Value My wife and I spent two nights in Barcelona and were very pleased with our stay at the Hotel Pulitzer. I decided on this hotel based on a lot of research, including the Trip Advisor feedback.The hotel is perfectly located with easy access to all the major attractions by walking, subway or cab. The rooms are very comfortable and well furnished. As others have said, they are narrower than we are used to and modern isn't to everyone's taste but our room with King bed was very clean, well appointed with all the things we like (robes, slippers, safe, etc.) and very spacious overall. It's the staff that makes or breaks a hotel and the Pulitzer has a great one. Everyone we met was extremely helpful. They gave us an excellent map, sightseeing directions, made restaurant recommendations (excellent) and reservations and made sure we had a cab for an early morning flight. All of this was done with a smile. They were very gracious in allowing me to try to speak my poor Spanish (I didn't even try Catalonian) but were also willing to rescue me in excellent English when I struggled.Our room included breakfast, which was excellent and we enjoyed a cocktail or two at the bar. We were sorry that the roof top bar had closed for the season but maybe next time.The Hotel Pulitzer is a great hotel in a perfect location with a wonderful staff that provides exception value for the money.

<Content>Great hotel, great service Stayed one night pre-cruise on 28th September. <Author>MariaGIreland
<Content>Your decision should be easy! Brilliant! I have just returned from a two-night stay in the Hotel Pulitzer in Barcelona. Our decision to choose this hotel was based on the reviews seen on Tripadvisor and most especially on the very genuine replies inserted by the hotel Manager. I did untold research regarding hotels for this trip as it was a very special trip for both myself and my sister. I wanted everything to be perfect with no time wasted fixing any mistakes or carrying out any re-working of our plans. We were not disappointed! We had a fantastic trip and this was definitely enhanced by this superb hotel. I actually feel quite hesitant recommending it as we wanted to keep it all to ourselves but that didn't seem fair!The location is perfect. It is literally a few steps from the central Placa de Catalunya. This proved to be an invaluable location as we were within walking distance of many of the main sights and on the route for the red and blue Bus Turistica (worth using, definitely if you are short on time). The hotel is situated on a quiet side street......so no noise at night!The staff in the hotel are very friendly (in a very understated, gentle, smiley way which we loved!) and extremely professional and efficient. The superb customer service actually started before we left Ireland at all! I had been researching the vast array of restaurants available in the city and became more and more confused. I eventually narrowed the list down to about 6 and couldn't make up my mind betwen them all. Because of the Manager's very genuine comments on this website, I decided that I could probably trust him to set us straight......and I was right! Within a day, I was contacted with restaurant suggestions for each night. I decided on two, and these were subsequently booked for us by Patricia at the front desk. No hassle, no problem just friendly, efficient service. What a pleasure!On arrival, we were greeted by Sergio at the front desk.He was very pleasant, friendly and efficient. (If you find that I am repeating my adjectives, that is because there are not enough to do justice to the standard of this hotel). Our check-in was handled quickly, our restaurant reservations were confirmed and we were given little appointment cards for each.Our room was excellent. I had thought that our room would actually be smaller so we were both pleasantly surprised by the space we had, The room is very trendy and modern, but most of all comfortable. There is excellent and smart use of the available space with your every possible need catered for. The suitcases fit underneath the bed; there is ample wardrobe and drawer/shelf space; the lights are controlled with switches which you keep depressed so as to alter the lighting levels in a slow manner and thus you can easily control the level of lighting you prefer. There is aircon, a lovely shower, a large mirror in the bedroom and a make-up mirror in the bathroom. We were provided with bath-robes and slippers and ample, very nice, toiletries. The beds were very comfortable. To avoid boring you, the room was more than perfect for our needs and exceeded expectations in terms of comfort. It IS narrow but definitely there is enough space so as not to be restrictive.After our return from the restaurant on the first night (El Passadis del Pep........HIGHLY RECOMMENDED), we retired to the hotel bar for a drink. The bar is very relaxing and is decorated as per the rest of the hotel....clean, crisp lines with modern , trendy furniture. The atmosphere is very mellow and added to the feeling that this hotel was fast becoming our home from home.The staff here were very pleasant and again helpful.We decided to have breakfast in the hotel for the sake of convenience and that was the correct decision! For 鈧?5, we had unlimited access to eggs, mushrooms, cheeses, stuffed tomatoes, fruits, yoghurts, various breads, various pastries, coffees etc etc. What a spread for that price. The staff here were again very friendly and attentive. The man on duty was particularly excellent as he really tried to make sure that we wanted for nothing. He was very gentle in his attitude and made us feel right at home. Fully fortified we headed off for our day but returned in the early evening for a drink on the outside terrace. After our meal that night (L'Olive.....again we would recommend this restaurant.....just go easy on the breads at the start. We overdid it a bit and found the subsequent courses hard going! Try the sole catalan style.....) we returned to the hotel bar for a night cap which again, provided a perfect end to a perfect day. A taxi was ordered for us for our early start the next morning and this arrived a little early, which suited us perfectly. The efficiency just went on and on.......... We would both HIGHLY recommend this hotel to anyone going to Barcelona.This is based on the staff, the hotel ambience and decor, the location and the facilities. We will return without a doubt and would not even bother researching accommodation again. Thank you Mr. Sanchez and all your staff for a magnificent stay. See you again some time.

The hotel is a boutique-style hotel with lovely common areas. The rooms are a little small but very adequate and modern. The free Wi-Fi was a real plus. The front desk staff were very helpful during our stay, especially Andrea and Ivker. Two restaurants that we really enjoyed during our stay were: Cuines Santa Caterina and Senyor Parellada. A highlight of our trip was a day tour by mini-van to Girona and the Costa Brava coast (Palafrugell) with Rabbies tours (www.rabbies.eu.com).

<Author>TheTraveller_1975
<Content>Our third visit .. We arrived in Barcelona on Monday around midday and we checked into the Pulitzer for the third time since 2004. Check in was seamless thanks to Sergio, and our room was all ready for us. The weather in Barcelona was unlike anything I have experienced there before, but thanks to the front desk staff lending us an umbrella we decided to venture outside. Over the course of our stay the weather did not improve so we spent most of our time in the hotel. Given the extensive wine, liquor and cocktail menus on offer this was a pleasure and not a downside to our trip. The staff were mostly attentive, however the bar staff duing the day left a little to be desired. We have travelled all over the world and stayed in many fantastic hotels - and this is one of the best in our opinion. All in all the Pulitzer offers fantastic contemporary rooms, free wi-fi (which is quite unusual), and a great atmosphere. We will definitely be back, and also plan to visit the new Pulitzer in Rome !

<Author>Azulann
<Content>Three nights before our cruise I fell in love with Barcelona , in part do to the Hotel Pulitzer. We arrived from the USA at noon and our rooms were ready for us. I, as a single person ,was traveling with two couples. I did receive a single room rate. The location is perfect. At the end of the block is Plac de Catalunya, gateway to a number of neighborhoods to explore on foot,and the access to La Rambla.The front desk staff were so helpful. We received a map and a tour book upon arrival. They helped us with recommendations for dinner, got us taxis, found out the Mass times at the Cathedral,suggested streets to explore nearby.The bar/wait staff were also very helpful and friendly. Hotel staff are the first people one meets in a foreign city and they can set the tone for the whole stay.All of our rooms had the same layout. Clean, high ceilings, wonderful beds, sleek bathrooms with nice amenties. Loved the bathrobe and slippers. Rooms facing the front had large windows and small balcony to observe the street below.Great variety at the breakfast buffet. Nice outside seating area. I loved the lobby bar , understated modern elegance. Best of all was the roof top terrace, for drinksand conversation after a full day of sightseeing.I will be back to Barcelona and will definitely stay at the Pulitzer again.

<Author>MaskedRider
<Content>Fantastico Just came back from a short trip to Barcelona. Stayed at the Hotel Pulitzer, which had a fantastic location, just off the Place de Catalunya. Great for the bus tours around the city.The hotel is boutique style, is clean and very nicely decorated and furnished. Our room was a standard double room, had all the expected requirements from shower gel to bath robes, tv to balcony. The room was furnished to a high standard and very modernly decorated. The hotel has two bars and a restaurant. The food was reasonably priced and looked good in the restaurant although we did not eat there, only because we wanted to explore further afield. The hotel has a roof top bar which is the most amazing place to chill out after a hectic day exploring Barcelona. We spent a couple of nights up there and the staff were excellent, even if they did not have what you wanted, they would go to the bar within the hotel to get it. I would recommend this hotel for a stay in Barcelona because of price, location, and quality. Overall i would give this hotel 9 out of 10 (there is always room for improvement).

<Author>Irish_Jen
<Content>The fabulous Pulitzer We have just returned from a fabulous weekend in Barcelona where we stayed in the wonderful Hotel Pulitzer.The location is first class - right in the heart of the city - stones throw from Las Ramblas (if you want it!), and walking distance to the old town and the port. We got the aerobus (only 鈧?,05 one way) which drops you in the Place de Catalunya - the hotel is a 2 min walk from here... so no need for a taxi. Oh... and there's a Starbucks right at the end of the street :)The staff spoke excellent English and were extremely helpful. The hotel itself is an oasis of calm with wonderful funky music playing in the background of the lobby and bar area. The bar is kitted out with huge white leather sofas - great to flop into after a lengthy day of sightseeing. The room was long and narrow, but very well presented. The bathroom was lovely with the expected little extras. The bed was one of the most comfortable hotel beds I have ever encountered.If you're a couple, get the 'Romance Package' with breakfast included in the price and a bottle of Cava delivered to your room on your first evening.If I was returning to Barcelona, I wouldn't look past the Hotel Pulitzer.

<Author>MikeGrimsby
<Content>Ideal Base in Barcelona We chose this hotel for our first trip to Barcelona based on the recommendations on this site, and were delighted with it. It was very easy to get to from the Aerobus stop, and the location would be hard to beat - we walked nearly everywhere.We had a standard room at the back of the hotel - nice and quiet. Found the size of room fine, and liked the style of decor. The bed was as comfortable as any we've ever slept on. I do personally like a bedside clock, which wasn't present, but that's a very minor quibble. The aircon seemed very quiet, in some hotels I can find this a problem at night.All the staff we came into contact with were charming. Breakfast met our needs well, and we thought the one lunch we had in the hotel was good value at 20Euros - including a glass of wine and coffee.We enjoyed the rooftop bar - after our miserable English summer it was very pleasant to sit outside in the evening and be warm!We only had three days in Barcelona, so only got to see a fraction of the sights. When we return to see more, I'm sure we'll stay at the Pulitzer again.

<Author>Fridaysmom
<Content>Somewhat disappointing Based on previous reviews, I had high expectations for this hotel, but have to admit, similar to the previous review, that I was somewhat disappointed with this hotel. The lobby area, dining room and roof-top bar are all very nice, but the rooms are very small! We had even decided to book the 'superior room' as we knew that the rooms were small, but it also was very narrow and the only difference between this room and the standard room appeared to be the addition of a small couch. The width of the room, however, appeared to be similar, which me feel quite claustrophobic. As previously noted, there was little space to get by the t.v. on the wall to the desk area (you actually had to duck down to get by), and the sitting area by the desk was also quite cramped. We did have a small balcony, but couldn't figure out how to open the door. Similar to the previous reviewer, we were given no instructions on the room when our luggage was brought up.We also arrived from overseas around 11 am and were told that because other guests in the room wouldn't be checking out until noon that the room wouldn't be ready until around 2 (or possibly 1 at the earliest). We checked our luggage and tried to entertain ourselves, but after an hour of walking around returned to the lobby in the hopes that we could get into the room early. After listening to rather annoying new wave music for nearly 2 hours, we were finally let into our room at 1:55 pm. I have to admit that I was quite disappointed that no efforts were made to attend to our room to accommodate the fact that we had been traveling all night to get to Barcelona.We had also booked the romantic package, but despite previous reference to red bows and rose petals all we got was a bottle of cava delivered to our room.Positives of the hotel include a great location (close to the Ramblas and to several metro stops), very friendly staff (who helped with restaurant recommendations--including a very good nearby tapas bar), free internet, a good breakfast buffet, and a nice roof-top bar (we did not have a drink there though). I haven't stayed in other hotels in Barcelona so don't know how this compares, but I would not rate this hotel as anything special as compared to hotels that I have stayed at in other major cities around the world.

<Author>dlr6067
<Content>Not the luxury expected Arrived Sunday after an early morning flight and a busy Saturday night for the hotel, so as we expected we were not able to check in. We were provided with a map of the city, and we checked our luggage. Unfortunately it was raining, we were exhausted and with little else to do on a Sunday AM we sat in the lobby/lounge for about an hour waiting out the rain. Returned to the hotel at 1 and were told our room was ready. We were brought up to a room right off the elevator, which normally I would have asked to switch from, but we were so exhausted we looked forward to a nap. The bellman brought our luggage behind us, but provided no introduction to the room. Maybe its because we were tired but it took us a minute to figure out the bathroom door was a slider, and that the safe was inside the desk. We pulled the drapes for a nap, and there were little pinprick holes throughout them that let in light; I'm not thinking these were intentional. So much for the soundproof rooms...housekeeping was so noisy right outside our room all afternoon, and there was noise from the street outside, so we were unable to sleep. Then at 7, there was a knock on the door with our cava (we booked the romantic package); apparently room service did not see the do not disturb sign (he did apologize), but we finally gave up trying to sleep. The front desk provided us with a very good recommendation for tapas, and we headed out to enjoy the city. We enjoyed a drink in the hotel's rooftop bar, which is worth a stop, and the bartender was very informative and nice to talk to.  The room was very narrow, as noted by other reviewers, and the bathroom tile was stained to the point that my husband thought it hadn't been cleaned in a while. The breakfast provided a good selection, but all the hot food was cold because they didn't use warmers. All in all, our stay was not up to the level we expected with this hotel being rated best luxury in Barcelona. We stayed at another hotel upon our return to Barcelona a week later, right on Las Ramblas, and found it nicer, a little less expensive and it was actually quieter despite the location.

<Author>www.chubbyhubby.net
<Content>Classy Hotel, Great Location I travel at least a week every month, so I see a lot of hotels. I also stay in a lot of boutique hotels. So, I don't get impressed too easily.My wife and I just came back from a one week trip to Catalonia. We spent the first two nights of our trip and the last at the Pulitzer. We liked the hotel a lot. It was chic, smart, clean, comfortable and well-designed.In order, here's what I liked best:1. Location! Right off Plaza Catalonia. Perfect. 10-15 walk to La Boqueria; 5 minute walk to Passeig de Gracia. You could not ask for a better location.2. Polite staff. The staff were all helpful and very charming, even when I was peppering them with dumb questions. I really admired that when my wife and I were waiting on the sidewalk outside of the hotel, for a friend to pick us up in a rented car, the security guy on duty made it a point to stand near us whenever suspicious characters came walking down the street.3. Smart contemporary and not over the top design. I am very sick of over-designed hotels. The pulitzer was classy. The lobby was chic and filled with cool-looking people our whole trip. The rooms, while nowhere near huge (this is Europe after all), were decorated smartly, with nice neutral and earthy tones.4. Smart design touches in the room. The foldaway desk was great since I needed to do some work on the trip but didn't want to be tripping over the desk at other times. The light switches by the beds were well-placed. The bathrooms were well laid-out and the amenities were nice. 5. Price. The hotel gave me a great rate so I couldn't have been happier. I got great value for money. I would stay at the Pulitzer again in a heartbeat. Happy travels!

<Author>skyejaden
<Content>Perfection in a perfect city I recently stayed at the Hotel Pulitzer from April 30 - May 7th. I chose it originally through reviews on this site and I couldn't have been more pleased. I am a female who traveled to Spain solo and met a friend there, so I chose it first and foremost on its ease of getting there by myself. It's just literally a minute or two walk to the A1 airport bus which is hands down the best way to get back and forth to the airport.The staff at the front desk were very courteous and kind with my limited knowledge of Spanish. There was a tiny mix up in the bed configuration, but they solved it quickly and check-in was a breeze.I had requested a room with a balcony facing the street and I'm happy that I did. It lets in a nice amount of fresh air. We never found a problem with heat or air conditioning - it was always perfect and easy to control.The beds were very comfortable to me, and the linens were super clean and fresh. The bathroom was extremely spacious with nice touches and amenities. The shower was strong and hot water was never a problem. The whole room was very clean and smelled really nice. The design of it was very pretty with the dark colors and artwork and the flat screen on the wall was a plus, although the channels to choose from were not so great. But I didn't go to Spain to watch TV!While a lot of people have said the rooms are small, this is true but I never felt closed in at all. And Barcelona is a city to explore - not one to stay in the hotel room!! But upon return to it, it was a quiet calm haven to rest in. With two of us there, we didn't feel squeezed in at all. There's a spacious closet in which to place your suitcases and hang clothes.I didn't try the room service or the restaurants, as there are a bounty to choose from right outside the door. But I did get ice at the bar and they were happy to provide a bowl of it! I wouldn't hesitate at all to book this hotel again. It's location is far enough off of the Ramblas to be quiet, and close enough to walk two minutes and have your morning coffee there. It really couldn't be situated any better.

<Author>Fivestartraveller
<Content>Prizeworthy This was a two-day surprise visit to celebrate our engagement and overall we considered it a wonderful choice. The location is perfect - literally just off Plaza de Catalunia but in a relatively quiet street. The hotel has a more boutique feel with modern, understated decor, a truly fantastic roof terrace with lounge-about chairs, and stylish rooms that, although not huge, are beautifully decorated. The food in the bar was of a very high quality and a reasonable price and staff were always courteous.I opted for the romantic package on the first night and we arrived to find a bow tied around our door, champagne on ice, and rose petals scattered across the bed and in the bathroom - always goes down well with your newly elected fiancee!My only criticism would be that on two occasions the service from staff left a little to be desired - the girl in the restaurant got our order wrong completely (missed one item completely and gave us another dish we hadn't ordered). And on the evening I needed an ironing board I was told one would arrive in the room in 10 minutes. 30 minutes later it hadn't arrived and on phoning I could not get a response. Eventually I went down to reception and was told I would have to carry the ironing board and iron up to my room as they only had one person on reception at that time. Not a major issue but when you're paying four-star prices you perhaps expect a slightly better level of personal service. But then again my experience of Spanish service, in hotels and restaurants, is that they are generally more relaxed than in England, so maybe this slight upset isn't anything to pay much attention. Overall I would recommend the hotel highly - the staff were incredibly friendly and there's a fantastically relaxed atmosphere which really sets you up for your stay in Barcelona.

<Author>Angie00708
<Content>Great Location Just returned from a four day stay at the Pulitzer. We chose the hotel having read previous reviews and were not disappointed. You could walk straight past the hotel as it is not terribly showy on the outside and inside looks dark but as previous reviews have noted, the theme of the decor throughout is black, chocolate brown and white. We stayed in room 402 which is on the front and has a balcony. Yes the rooms are long and narrow but perfectly adequate. The bathroom is a good size and both bed linen and towels are sparkling white matched by the overall cleanliness of the hotel. We didn't have breakfast having read it was expensive but there must be thousands of cafes, tapas bars etc to choose from all within easy walking distance of the hotel. The lounge on the ground floor is very comfortable with plenty of sofas and we relaxed here a couple of times when it was raining outdoors. We were disappointed the roof terrace was not open - apparently undergoing work but when we went for a 'nose' to see what it was like there was no apparent work taking place. We caught the airport bus (A1) to and from the airport. Good value at 4 Euros and very reliable running every six minutes. the stop is immediately outside the terminal building. However when we got off the bus in Plasa de Catalunya it was quite late and we were not prepared for just how big this square is. If you do catch bus the street you need is opposite where you get off bus in between Habitat (FNAC building) and the BBBV clock tower building. Believe it or not we wondered around for half an hour dragging our suitcases before a kind local lady was able to point us in the right direction. All of the hotel staff we dealt with were very courteous and helpful and are a credit to the management. We didn't need to ask much of them but whenever we had a question they were very responsive. I would stay here again and would recommend the hotel to others. The location is a real asset to the hotel.  
<Date>Apr 20, 2008

<Author>decision
<Content>Great Location We stayed here at the beginning of April.We picked this hotel having read the reviews.The best part of this hotel is it's location. It's on a side street, turning left out of the hotel it's less than one minute's walk from Pl. Catalunya and turning right it's less than one minute from a Starbucks cafe.Room : We were not fortunate enough to get an upgrade as others did, so we had the basic room which is quite small width wise without the couch but with one armchair. The television is on the wall facing the bed and every time we passed it we felt we were going to hit our heads. The lighting is very nice and you can dim them if you are in the mood which is a nice touch. There are robes and slippers provided. The bathroom is very nice with nice fluffy towels and shower gel, shampoo and moisturiser provided. There is also a man and woman box which has a toothbrush, toothpaste, razor, etc. but one thing missing is cotton buds which is usually provided in 4* hotels. We booked the romance package which included breakfast and a bottle of cava. For anyone else booking this package, apparently the cava is delivered to the room around 7pm in ice bucket with two champagne glasses. We had to ask when it would be delivered. If we hadn't and only returned to our room late after eating, I would imagine the cava would have been warm at that stage. Our room was on the 5th floor to the back of the hotel which got the sun for most of the day, looked down on the back of the hotel and onto the next street on which C  A is located. There was no balcony but the window doors opened in with a railing outside. If you are to the front of the hotel, there is a very small balcony with standing room only. The street is not very wide and you only get the sun in the evening.Breakfast : This is served until 11am during the week, later at the week-end. It comprises of juices, cereals (no cornflakes), cold meats, cheeses, fresh fruits, scrambled eggs, mini saugages, crispy bacon, bread rolls, bread to be toasted, yogurts, danish pastries and doughnuts.We arrived down for breakfast at 10.30am to see a waitress taking plates of what looked like really nice shortcake cookies, we presumed to a different location in the breakfast room. We soon realised that they were clearing away and these were not available when we would have liked them with our coffee and tea to finish. If you like coffee there's no problem but if you like tea, like me, they bring a cup of warm water and a tea bag. You get the milk from the large jug for the cereal. Most 4* star hotels we have stayed in have teapots and small jugs for cold milk which make it much more user friendly. Pulitzer Management please take note.Restaurant : Not open Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday nights.Having stayed previously in the AC Diplomatic which is a further 5/10 mins away from Pl. Catalunya, We are still undecided which is better overall!!!!  
<Date>Apr 9, 2008

<Author>KELor
<Content>A Lovely Hotel! My daughter and I stayed at the Pulitzer for 6 nights. Upon arrival, we were told that our room had been upgraded which was a wonderful surprise! The room, which was immaculate, was long but rather narrow and was in the front of the building. The beds were quite comfortable and had great linens (duvet cover changed every day, etc.) We also had a comfortable sofa. I loved the hardwood floors- they just added to the feeling of cleanliness. We could hear some street noise late at night, but after all- we were in the middle of Barcelona! The bathroom was also very clean. The front desk was pleasant and helpful.The location couldn't be better- we walked almost everywhere, and it helped to be so centrally located. My only complaint was the cost of breakfast at 15 Euros each. This is fine if one wants to have a large breakfast. However, we both were quite ill with food poisoning (we think from some seafood eaten at what we thought was a lovely restaurant down by the water). On our last 2 days, we only ate a roll, butter and tea, and we were told by the server that we still had to pay 30 Euros plus tax- there are no exceptions. I thought this policy was unreasonable. Had we felt better, we would have tried to find another place, but honestly we were too sick. We were also charged 2 Euros to bring a small dish of ice to our room when we were unable to even get out of bed. I know that's only $3, but it was the principle. We tried to have toast sent up one afternoon, which appeared to be a major request. It finally entailed a trip to the front desk to beg, as we were unable to eat anything else. I'd like to think this was due to language difficulties :) All things considered, it was a good trip, and we will probably stay here when we visit Barcelona again- hopefully in the near future.

<Author>Jet-Setter-SF
<Content>Better than average artsy hotel I stayed at the Pulitzer for a big conference and chose the hotel solely for the fact that it was the only mid-price hotel available in town. Later I learned it had great reviews on tripadvisor.com, and I was not disappointed.There was some problems with the room: specifically, the lighting controls were weird and hard to manage and master, and oddly the shower head flew off repeatedly when the water was turned on. There was no fix for the lighting, but the hotel quickly fixed the shower head problem. (Nice touch: the shower head was placed high on the wall -- nice for us tall folk.) Another weird issue -- the bar soap was tiny and smelly. I expect more from a high-end hotel.Otherwise, the room was fairly design-y. Dark wood floors, dark wood furniture, and a firm (comfortable) bed. One down-side of the dark wood everywhere was the lack of lighting in or near the closet. I was constantly afraid of leaving something behind in the drawers or on the shelves. The electric outlets in the room for charging cell phones and plugging-in laptops were not easy to reach, but the in-room safe was big enough for my 15 Macbook.Good things about the room: minibar was fairly inexpensive (2,20 euros for water) and free WiFi in the rooms. All rooms in the front of the hotel had small balconies overlooking the street with a view to Placa Catalunya down the street.My Wallpaper* guide to Barcelona mentioned that rooms 306 and 506 had extra space and a leather couch. I can vouch that 406 had the same extra space and couch. Nice and big, but a weird lay out in the long thin rectangular room. However, the fire escape map on the room door showed that most rooms were tiny. Be warned. Ask for one of the bigger rooms. As for the common areas, the bar area looked comfy although I did not take advantage. The breakfast buffet was great and included in my 300 euro room rate, so I can't comment on the value. I did not get room service, but I believe it was 24 hour service.Location-wise, it was quite convenient to Las Ramblas and the #1 underground metro line. And if you have to get to the hotel from the airport and there's a huge line for taxi's, the #17 bus from the airport stops just a block from the hotel (1,40 euros I think). (I usually do take the taxi, but in this case had to find an alternative method of transport!)All in all, I'd go back.  
<Date>Feb 25, 2008

<Author>Dominey
<Content>Great boutique hotel 鈥?would definitely stay here again We loved this hotel, very modern, clean and stylish in a great location, just of Placa Catalana. The communal areas with large white sofas are great to relax and sip a cocktail before an evening out. There is also a roof terrace bar that unfortunately was not open in Feb - a good reason to return again in summer! Our room was on the 4th of 5 floors, accessed via a glass elevator with dizzy views down to the bar area. The room was a fair size, not huge but fine for a weekend stay. There was a large bathroom with a deep bath (many hotels I've stayed in Barcelona have only had a shower or half bath) nice robes, slippers  toiletries. We couldn't get the temperature right in the room, it was rather warm throughout our stay - but couldn't be bothered to report it to reception so can't really complain!We had the room service breakfast which was a generous size, we didn't eat in the restaurant - although it looked very nice, with an outdoor terrace - so can't comment on the food.The staff were very helpful, booked us tables at restaurants, laundry and taxis. We will definitely stay here again.

<Author>Respilosa
<Content>Very stylish, good location The Hotel Pulitzer is very aesthetically pleasing. I'm a terrible snob about interior design, but could find no fault with the Pulitzer's tasteful decor. It made me happy.We were given the smallest room, which also had a large pillar blocking the middle of the space, but it was still an attractive, cozy, romantic place to collapse after a long day of walking. At 120 Euros a night, it was also a good enough value not to matter.Our one complaint about the room was the heat. Others have also mentioned it in their reviews of the hotel: the a/c doesn't work in the Winter, but the sun is strong enough on the southern side of the building that our room was unbearably hot unless we kept the windows open all night and the blackout curtains drawn all day. We weren't bothered by traffic noise, but a very light sleeper probably wouldn't do well with open windows. I recommend requesting a room that doesn't face south.The hotel's location off the Placa Catalunya is great for exploring all directions of the city on foot. The hotel bar is a very nice place to relax and have a few drinks. We also had a midnight meal there. The food was tasty, healthy and reasonably priced. The hotel charges 15 Euros for breakfast, but cheap and delicious coffee, xocolata and breakfast is available around the corner just inside the FNAC department store. Perhaps not the prettiest setting, but it's also not at all touristy, it's quick, and they do offer very good quality.

<Author>irishnomad
<Content>Great location but shame about the bathroom This hotel is in a fabulous location for exploring the city. 10 secs from Place de Catalunya. Aerobus and tourist bus leave from/arrive to here so it was more than handy. If you're a shopping fanatic it's also a great area with both Cortes Ingles within feet of each other and Las Ramblas just around the corner. Some great small boutiques down the side streets here.When we arrived we were shown to a smoking room which didn't suit. There were no indications of preferences when booking on the site so we just assumed that it would be non-smoking. We went back down to reception and were given a new room straight away. Although we were asked if we had used anything in the room which I found a bit unnecessary as we had literally been there for 2 mins.Otherwise I found the staff courteous and pleasant.Overall the room was lovely. Great design in some areas and made the most of the space. Bathroom overall was nice but the only thing that let it down was the staining on the marble tiles as mentioned in previous reviews. The thing is that the bathroom was spotless otherwise but the staining probably looked worse that it actually was. I'm sure there's some kind of cream to improve this.....The new room we were given unfortunately didn't have the view of the previous one of the side street. Instead it looked out over the main street and the breakfast room/terrace. The main street was quite noisy but you soon got used to it. Also you could hear the odd peep from the other rooms and the hall especially when they were wearing heels!Breakfast was good. No complaints here. Room was nice and bright and terrace was lit up at night. It was while we were here that we realised where the music was coming from which woke us up each morning when we had the door open. Not great but we were getting up anyway.Lobby very nice too. Lovely rioja and great atmosphere.One of the only times I've had room service in a hotel and it was fantastic! We had the burgers and they were just what we wanted. Recommended if you're feeling a little tired and can't be bothered to go in search of food.I would stay here again but I would ask for a room on the other side of the hotel as to avoid street and breakfast noise and I would also hope that they had found something to improve the tiles in the bathroom just for appearances sake.

<Author>kipabelson
<Content>The Pulitzer is a winner! We stayed at the Pulitzer over the Christmas holiday. Above all, the location of the hotel is utterly fantastic. You are 50 yards from Placa de Catalunya where every mode of transportation is available. And, a whole bunch of interesting streets, shops and restaurants are within walking distance from there. The service at the hotel is outstanding and very accommodating. Every question that we asked was answered with enthusiasm and if the answer was not immediately known, they followed up on all of them. Our room was very small but pretty stylish. Despite the small room, the bed was a generous queen sized and extremely comfortable. The plumbing and climate control definitely needs work. The shower was so hot on some occasions that if we actually had gone under the water we probably would have burned ourselves. And since the air conditioning had been turned off for the winter, the room initially was very warm. However, when we told the desk about that, they shut off the heat in our room and by opening the window near the bed, the room was very cool and comfortable. My only real complaint about the hotel was the bar. Again, the bar area is very cool and stylish, but we were charged three different prices for the same drink order on different occasions. I thought the food in the city was pretty good, but there is no question in my mind that tapas is the way to go. And, there is no shortage of tapas restaurants. One of our favorites was on Avenida de Catalunya and was called Cuitat Comtal. It was a really fun and active place. Great tapas. Try the cuttlefish if it is available. And the white anchovies are great. Overall, Barcelona and the Hotel Pulitzer are great.

<Author>mmctrip
<Content>Overall A nice hotel I stayed at this hotel for 6 nights in November. Upon arrival you are given an excellent book of tourist routes and restaurant reviews by the staff . This was very helpful. I had a room on the 4th Floor with two twin beds pushed together. The room was long and narrow with a nice bathroom (bath/tub combo). The toiletries were very nice (shampoo etc, nice creams (face and foot) and toothpaste/brush). There was a plasma TV and minibar. The bed was very comfortable. I did find the hotel very clean. The location was great. It is at the top of the Placa de Catalunya so it is close to the sites and to the aerobus. I was able to walk along the Paseo de Gracia at night for tapas and during the day I headed south to enjoy all the great sites. The Bus turistic is right by the hotel (a minute or so). I did not eat at the restaurant as I preferred a small breakfast so cannot comment on the restaurant. With respect to the noise issue mentioned by other posters, the room did face the courtyard where the bar is located. There was some minor noise from the bar (plates being stacked) but not enough to bother or keep me awake. After a certain time in the evening it was clear that the staff were making every effort to be quiet. If you are a light sleeper you could request a room away from the courtyard but quite frankly I was so tired from all the sightseeing and I confess the great food/wine in Spain that I fell asleep right away! The only issue I had was that the safe in the room did not work. To be fair the staff at the front desk called the technician right away and it was replaced the second day while I was out and I was able to store my passport etc for the rest of my stay. I would recommend this hotel to those wanting a nice, clean central hotel in this beautiful city.

<Author>civetta11
<Content>Impressive service (and patience!) by Reception Manager Stayed for 3 nights prior to Mediterranean cruise, booked Superior room for parents and Standard twin room for brother  myself. For the Standard room we were allocated a room with handicap facilities (we were told the hotel sells this room as a standard room). We were offered another room where the 2 single beds were placed close together with a gap of no more than 4 inches, which isn't the most convenient for adult brother  sister. We were shown another room which also had the 2 single beds close together, but we appreciated being offered the choice. In the end, the Reception Manager suggested to move the bedside table in between the 2 beds and even moved the furniture himself with the help of a junior staff. All was sorted within minutes. A good selection of breakfast is offered in the airy, bright room of the restaurant. Location of hotel is excellent, close by Plaza Cataluyna/ Ramblas. The hotel arranged for a flamenco dinner show (surprisingly good) for us one night and a private city tour with an exceptional English-speaking guide. All in all, an excellent stay and highly recommended!

<Author>CarbonOffset
<Content>Good Location, Great Service We booked this hotel for a conference trip after reading reviews on TripAdvisor. The reviews were accurate - the hotel staff were the best I have encountered in a long time. They were helpful at all times, were able to recommend restaurants and bars to suit us and our plans, gave accurate directions, lent us an iron and ironing board, and kept the rooms and common areas very clean.The location of the hotel is excellent - it is a short walk to Las Ramblas and the Barri Gotic, a moderate walk to the shopping in L'Eixample, a department store/supermarket (El Corte Ingles) is within 3 minutes, and the metro line to the CCIB conference centre runs from Passeig de Gracia station, about 5 minutes walk away.As we were there on business, computer facilities were important. Wireless internet is free in this hotel. We were able to use the printers in the Hotel Regina next door.The room was long and narrow compared to other hotels, but there was enough space. The desk is only a fold down door on the cabinet in the room corner. There is a room safe. Many of the rooms open onto the atrium that stands above the lobby bar. This was noisy on the weekend night only, until about midnight. The front door of the room did not block out noise of the cleaning staff or neighbour's doors opening, but we have had similar (and worse) problems in other hotels in Barcelona.Breakfast cost 15 euros. I ate at one of many cheaper cafes nearby.

<Author>Canada_One
<Content>Pulitzer OK - But Poor Housekeeping I booked the Pulitzer based on Trip ratings, and while many aspects of the hotel were in fact quite good, there was a couple of things that cause me to rate as only average. To details.We booked a superior room, which does in fact have quite a bit more space than a regular room. All rooms are somewhat narrow and long. The nice flat screen TV's are mounted at the end of the bed, but you have to duck around it to access the other side of the bed.Best part of the Pulitzer is the decor, which is very hip and cool. Our room had great artwork very nicely framed and presented. It also had a great huge sliding door from the room to the bathroom, which had a very modern feel with full natural stone sink, floors and such. A nice leather couch was part of the superior room layout.Only downside was either due to poor selection of stone for the bathroom, or poor cleaning, hard to tell which. Unfortunately the lovely bathroom sink area had round glass stains all over it, and the floor had many water spot stains by the tub. This marred what could have been a true 4 star hotel room. There was also what looked like coffee spill stains on the wall by the bed. This could all have been easily fixed by a coat of paint and buffing of the stone in the bathroom.The lobby and bar on the ground floor is very nice, with white leather everywhere and a nice feel to the place.The location of the hotel was perfect for sighseeing in Barcelona, and just off the major thoroughfare enough so that noise was not an issue. Other than the bed being too hard for my liking (my wife loved it), sleeping was no problem at all. Other than Andrea, who was exceptionally helpful, unfortunately the rest of the front desk staff was clueless when it came to assistance. One desk member suggested a cab was necessary to get to a restaurent that was clearly only a 10 minute walk down one of the largest and most travelled streets in the city. The front desk staff seemed very young, and not very well trained. My advice is to seek out Andrea for recommendations and assistance. Although the Pulitzer was good value to money, and had a great location and many positives, I would look for something else next time I was in Barcelona. This is mainly due to the unfortunate staining of the bathroom surfaces and the walls. This is really not acceptable for a 4-star hotel.

<Author>GTaylorNYC
<Content>A Strong Recomendation Dear Fellow Travellers:Greetings -- please see the letter below, which I wrote to the owner/president of the Hotel Pulitzer and which describes a recent incident my girlfriend and I encountered on the road to Barcelona and how the people at this hotel made a very bad situation much better. We are frequent travellers but have never encountered a hotel quite like this one, which is why I am posting this letter for everyone's benefit (my first posting ever). Happy trails! G TaylorSeptember 25, 2007Dear Mr. Roig: Please forgive us for not speaking Spanish.On June 21 of this year, we were attacked by bandits on the interstate just outside of Barcelona . The thieves cut our tire, held us up, and stole my girlfriend鈥檚 purse containing her passport, wallet, credit cards, cash, and irreplaceable personal items. One of the worst experiences of either of our lives.We quickly rushed to the nearby toll booth to call the police, but were told by the attendant to go to the police station in the city square. We parked the car close to the square and frantically ran into the Hotel Pulitzer to ask to use their phone to cancel our credit cards and to ask directions to the police station. As you could imagine, we were very shaken up and very emotional, especially as neither of us had ever been robbed before. Mr. Luis Carasa and Mr. Jose Sanchez calmly and professionally asked what had happened to us, and then allowed us to use the hotel鈥檚 staff phones to cancel our credit cards, free of charge and undisturbed. They also brought us refreshments and helped us to calm down. Mr. Carasa and Mr. Sanchez then offered to allow us to stay in the hotel at a special rate (we learned later that this took some juggling). This was both of our first time to Barcelona, and the mugging is an isolated event, but the kind actions of your Mr. Carasa and Mr. Sanchez afterwards went a long way to make such a bad occurrence better. They both went out of their way to help us in our time of need. We are both very grateful to these two gentlemen and the Hotel Pulitzer for the kindness and exemplary service we were given during such a bad situation. Mr. Carasa and Mr. Sanchez are a shining example of the many good things about Barcelona , and because of their actions, we would gladly return to Barcelona and would gladly stay in your hotel again (but where else?).Sincerely,G Taylor and J Sander  
<Date>Sep 27, 2007

<Author>I'mcomingback
<Content>Expectations exceeded I found the Hotel Pulitzer here on TA. It seemed to be in the perfect location for exploring Barcelona and the hotel itself looked like somewhere I'd like to stay.My expectations were far exceeded.First, I was extrememly impressed with the managers habit of responding to every review here on TA. Also his invitation to reviewers to contact him if they were returning. I E-mailed him to tell him of my upcoming visit. I received a response very quickly asking if I had any special requests or needed anything.It is this kind of detail that makes this hotel so special.The Pulitzers location is perfect for exploring Barclona. It is directly off of Placa de Catalunya and is a few minute walk to the top of La Rambla and into the Gothic area. I had read in many reviews here that the rooms were small. I didn't find this to be true. While certainly not huge they were big enough for a plesant stay. All of the rooms I saw seemed to be the same size. They are long and narrow, There was a big wardrobe in my room with more than enough room for all of my clothes and my luggage. There was an arm chair at one end with a chest/desk unit with a safe. The bed was very comfortable and the bathroom was very well appointed and very comfortable. My room was spotlessly clean and the housekeepers did a great job everyday.This is a very modern design hotel with really nice attention to details. The lobby, bar area and restaurant are very nice and beautifully decorated. The staff of the hotel were extrememly nice and friendly. All of the people at the desk spoke English. They all worked hard to insure that my stay was a good one, meeting every request with a smile and helping in any way they could.I also have to mention the beautiful roof top terrace. Very comfortable with big couches and several seating areas.The two things that I read about in other reviews that I will agree with is the poor placement of the televisions and the tissue packets. I didn't find either to be a problem. This hotel is so nice, pack your own tissues.

<Author>Delta1978
<Content>Lovely hotel We stayed here in early September 2007. It's a gorgeous hotel - beautiful lobby, lounge, roof top bar. The room we stayed in was very nice and comfortable. Compared to other hotels in this price range, we found the room to be a bit small and were kind of navigating around our luggage as there wasn't a luggage rack or good place to store it other than the floor. The lighting system in the room was also a bit of a mystery....they were all set up on a dimmer kind of system but we could never quite figure out how to turn the light off we wanted without trying every light in the room. But the bed was very comfortable and the location couldn't be beat.A word of caution - and this is not intended to be positioned as the fault of the hotel - but watch your belongings very carefully. My husband and I stopped by the front desk to check a dinner reservation one night on our way out the door. My husband walked up to the desk and I took a seat on a bench / ottoman just off the lobby. I put my purse down beside me on the seat and watched what was going on at the desk. Within 2 minutes my purse was snatched without me noticing - and it was literally right beside me. The hotel is located just off Plaza Catalunya and a thief could easily cruise through a busy lobby and make their way out the door without anyone noticing in a matter of seconds and disappear into the crowded Plaza. Everyone knows to be extra careful out on the streets, but just a reminder to not let your guard down once you hit your hotel - an easy thing to do when the hotel is on the high end like this one.

<Content>Very nice hotel We arrived at about 11:30am and our room wasn't ready which was to be excepted before 12. We took a couple of bottles of wine from the local supermarket up there and the glasses from our room as we were a bit skint by the end of our trip, hee hee. The staff opened the bottle for us too which was nice as we didn't think we would be allowed taking our own food/drink up there. The hotel bar was a joke, very slow service, expensive and the staff don't know how to make the cocktails. That is probably why it was empty. Go to the Zurich Bar round the corner from the hotel at the top of The Ramblas (Very Nice). Lots of seating outside with reasonable prices. The location of the hotel couldn't be any better to be honest, extremely central. The rooms themselves were perfect, not a bad word to say about them. I would definately recommend this hotel to friends.

<Author>JSTPK
<Content>Very central location, but slightly gloomy. Central location and easy to find. Reception staff slightly haughty, no-one mentioned rooftop bar, so that still remains a slight mystery to me. The room was very clean and plenty enough room for a city break, but everything was so dark, obviously a style thing, but nonetheless slightly gloomy., especially as our view was onto a concrete wall and then C and A sign, so no natural light. I was travelling with my daughter (19) and felt that maybe it was more of a couples hotel. Have to say a little noisy in the mornings as rooms are situated around a central atrium which means the sound is carried upwards from the lounges on the ground floor and through the central hollow of the building through the upper levels of the sleeping accomodation. But on the whole very classy, reasonably priced accomodation for centre of big city and any faults are probably based on personal style taste.

<Author>HannaSweden
<Content>Great Hotel  The Pulitzer is located right next to La Rambla without feeling like it is too much in the middle of everything. The staff is really nice, always smiling and being helpful. The rooms are a bit small, but stylish with good wardrobe space. The only complaint about the room was that it was noisy, we heard the bartender talking like we where sitting next to him, yet, we were on the fifth floor, and the bar is on the fist... but it is an atrium. Ask for a room that is high up, and not with a door by the atrium.The breakfast is good by South European standards. It has a little bit of everything, enough to keep most people happy. Eggs, different bread, different cheeses, tortilla, ham, bacon, fruit and muesli and so on. There is also the possibility of having breakfast outdoors at the terrace, lovely on a sunny day!Conclusion, Great hotel to stay at in Barcelona. Not as fancy as The Omm, but also much cheaper. I would definitely go back!

<Author>Ddkent
<Content>Our favourite place in Europe The location of this hotel is fantastic - just around the corner from Las Ramblas.Like most European hotels, the rooms are small, but they are comfortable, modern and clean. In Spain, it means a room for two people, ie twin single beds. Thankfully, the staff were aware of this and asked us at check in, then changed us to another room.Very happy with every aspect of our stay. Did I mention the fantastic location?

<Author>MarkC51
<Content>So Suite...... Ssshhh........here's a secret. The Pulitzer has a Suite, and it's fabulous...Despite several hundred positive reviews, no one appeared to have stayed in anything other than a standard room. We wanted something different , as it was our 10th Wedding Anniversary. I looked on the Hotel website and noticed they had 1 Suite (only one) in the Hotel, and enquired about availability. It was fortunately available, and exceptional value at 310 Euros per night.We arrived on Thursday afternoon after a decent flight. The reception staff were very cheerful, and I had paid for a 'celebration package' for the room. This entailed roses, champagne, chocolates, breakfast in bed, and a nice hot bath to await us.We were given our key and shown to our room. Upon entering my wife (who suspected nothing) , was blown away. The room was beautiful, decked out in chocolate browns , whites and greys, and luxurious. The room was very large, with a 4 poster bed in the centre. It really could not be faulted.As if we weren't already delighted, I pulled back the curtains to reveal an amazing Terrace/balcony, which was just decadent. It was very large, decked in solid wood throughout, and had loungers , remote controlled awnings, plants and a large table. We felt like royalty. The bathroom also didn't disappoint. Whilst quite narrow, they had made best use of the space with some natural light, and both a wetroom and a bath. All fixtures and fittings were of the highest quality.There are numerous other things that I could mention, including a fabulous Denon Speaker system throughout the suite, which allows you to connect your ipod and enjoy music in the bathroom, bedroom and terrace. There's also a 42 plasma tv, and various books.Breakfast was good, pretty standard fare, but nice.The location is perfect, a stones throw from the market square and las ramblas. If you are looking to stay in Barca, and want to treat yourself, look no further. Believe the hype..

<Author>moveabout
<Content>Great Location / Tiny Rooms Our primary motivation for selecting this hotel for our weekend trip to Barcelona was the location and the expectation it had modern / comfortable rooms (as per the website).We booked through the hotel website (EUR 170.00 per night for two nights during July 2007) and felt quite satisfied with the price. We arrived and were warmly received at reception. The common area in the lobby / bar / restaurant were all very welcoming though by the time you walk up and down the first floor you can tell the hotel is 'squeezed in what is a relatively narrow building'. We were given a room on the 4th floor (I guess one of the cheap rooms??) which was very very small (I think most of the standard doubles are this small) but had most amenities you could think off. The bathroom is very narrow but had a very comfortable shower. The surfaces in the rooms (simple wooden furniture that passes as modern furniture) was losing its luster with small cracks in the veneer / paint. None of this is paritcularly distressing because we weren't intending on spending much more than nights in the room. Though we were content with the room we discovered much to our dismay that the worn feel of the room carried through to the lighting (which was a real pain to use, using gradient lighting knobs), where we could find no way of turning off our night lamps (they have no switches on the lamp, rather a wall gradient switch).We took out the lightbulb, went to sleep, and complained at reception. They were very quick to accomodate us in an upgraded room on a higher floor (which was still small but much more comfortable) and threw in breakfast on Sunday. Generally greatly relieved that the hotel had such a positive customer attitude we went off for sightseeing and shopping.One last problem occurred on Saturday night where the hotel's air conditioning broke down. We were told on Sunday that it was a general problem (not only our room) and we were fortunate it hadn't been a sweltering day (Barcelona can get hot and humid in summer). Our overall impression was great location, with quality of the room and its facilities hit or miss.

<Author>jellyb1
<Content>Amazing hotel - loved it! My partner and I came back from a 3 night stay at the Hotel Pulitzer this morning and I loved this hotel so much that wanted to write a review straight away.The hotel was absolutely fantastic. It is very modern and luxurious and spottless with very comfortable surroundings. There was free internet access in the room so we took our laptop along and really enjoyed being able to email home and sends pictures to all our friends and family to make them jealous.We used room service on several occassions and found the price very reasonable. The food was absolutely delicious and at a very high standard.The location of the hotel was fantastic. You could walk to a great number of attractions and a 1 minute walk from the main shopping street. We also used the many metro stops around the hotel to travel to different sights such as the Segrada Familia and found it so easy to travel around the city.We both agreed one of the best parts of this hotel were the staff. They were so helpful and couldn't do enough to make our stay an enjoyable one. They always recognised us and said hello even though it isn't a very small hotel. When we ordered a drink in the main lobby bar the bar staff seemed horrified that we would carry the drinks to the table ourselves and insisted on bringing them over. They were all just great.If you have any doubt about staying at this hotel then there really is no need. If I ever go to Barcelona again I will definately be staying at this hotel.

<Author>dawabbit
<Content>A cool haven in summer. HOtel Pulitzer is a calm retreat on a hot day. The cool neutrals of the air conditioned room were welcome. Even though our room overlooked a main street it was quiet, due to good soundproofing. The location is absolutely perfect! Not on the Ramblas, but right off it, near a central square etc., with fantastic shopping. Note: this hotel is not partnered with other hotel Pulitzers in Europe, so it must be judged on its own value.The lighting system was difficult for me to learn, although I am not a quick study in things like that. The bed was very, very comfortable and we slept well. A few strange things: Since the room was very tiny, there was one possilbe hazard for a person who gets up, half asleep in the middle of the night to use the bathroom. To get there, you need to go around the bottom of the bed (if you sleep in the right), and in traversing the 18 inch wide pathway to the facilities, is a wall mounted TV right at head level. I recommend turning the tv so it is a flat as possible so as not to break one's nose walking right into it. The only other quirk I found was that the female of the duo in the room was alloted a pack of two (yes two), tissues per person. Bring your own tissues. Overall, we were pleased with our stay and would return there without doubt.

<Content>Not Impressed... We stayed for 3 nights at the Hotel Pulitzer with our two sons. The rooms are quite small and minimally furnished -- for example, there isn't a stand-alone desk, rather, a fold out work station. The tv is tiny. There are no tissues in the bathroom -- you have to call housekeeping to bring you small packets. <Content>Comfortable, stylish and well-run I really liked the Pulitzer. The people behind the front desk were very helpful, especially Amanda, who is just lovely. We really appreciated Julian Rubio's advance e-mail restaurant reservations and advice. What a big help he was! Understandably, the room was not ready, but the front desk staff cound not have been more helpful, offering sightseeing and dining advice, and the promise to call our cell phone the moment the room became available. Luigi the bartender was very nice and entertaining, and the entire staff was very professional, yet extremely nice. The room was not large, but clean and nicely decorated, and it met our purposes. I look forward to returning to Barcelona, and will make the Hotel Pulitizer my base.Don

<Content>Family of 4 enjoys stay at Hotel Pulitzer We stayed here for 5 nights in March and then returned for one more night after travelling to Morocco for 8 days. We were travelling with our kids ages 11 and 14. The first 5 nights we had a superior room and the kids a standard room. The final one night we both had standard rooms. So, in all we stayed in 4 different rooms. They were all wonderful. We did like the extra space of the superior - it also had a couch, which was particularly helpful when the kids came into our room to hang out as we got ready. I will say we stayed in 3 different standard rooms and they were all configured a bit different, but all very nice. I would not hesitate to stay in one. We were a bit concerned about the comments of them being small, but really did not find it an issue. They all had nice closet and drawer space and a nicely appointed bathroom.The staff was all excellent. There did seem to be a discrepancy in our reservation when we first checked in, but everything was taken care of to our satisfaction. I think the fact that the manager clearly monitors the reviews here shows how much they are interested in making your stay the best.We loved the breakfast and the buffet breakfast - other than some small BB's we have stayed in Italy, definitely the best European breakfast buffet for a hotel. The breakfast staff was very helpful and friendly, always remembering our preferred morning drink.This is in an excellent location, we were able to walk to L'Eixample, Las Ramblas, Barri Gothic and El Born. Right near Placa Catalunya but on a nice quiet side street. Our rooms were facing the street and we never had any noise problems. We all loved this place and hope to return soon!

<Author>rweidemx
<Content>Chinese design and Catalan hospitality We stayed at the Pulitzer for the special occasion of my wife's birthday for 3 nights at the end of March. As far as our adult son was accompanying us, we booked a double and a single room, which were arranged from the hotel right next to each other. We love boutique hotels with minimalistic design much better than faceless hotels of big chains, where a hotel room in NYC looks exactly the same like in any other place of the world. The interiour of the hotel is inspired by Chinese themes, and it uses the colors black and white (with a red dot in the bar, which is the central point of the hotel). From all the positive comments, given on this website, we would like to underline the ones, referring to the personnel, running the hotel. The staff is well selected, everybody is absolutely confident about his job, everything is smooth running, which is the result of real team work and a manager, who is open for comments and suggestions. All employees with customer contact (front desk, restaurant, bar) speak excellent English, and you will receive a smile, which goes right into your heart. This smile is very special, because it is natural. It shows, that everybody in the hotel loves his job every day, and that you as a customer are really welcome.We have stayed at other design hotels before, and we observed more than one time that cool hotel design triggers a cool attitude of the personnel, which can be interpreted as arrogant - this was absolutely not the case in the Pulitzer!Reading some complaints about street noise, clapping doors and rain drops falling onto the terrace roof we would like to admit, that yes, Barcelona is a big city, and the hotel is centrally located, but in a side street. Those, who are extremely noise sensitive, can make use a beautifully designed suite on the 6th floor, where complete privacy is guaranteed, the door of the suite will be the only door clapping, and possible rain drops will fall on the private terrace of the suite. However, we liked our rooms on the third floor, and we will definitely return to the Pulitzer.Big compliments to the entire hotel team. Keep on going this way, and you will be rewarded by guests, that take best memories home to their countries and that return to your hotel again and again!

<Author>fyffes
<Content>A brilliant weekend break! We stayed at the Pulitzer on 8th March for 3 nights. Everything was thoroughly enjoyable, and of the best quality. The room was extremely comfortable, breakfast selections were plentiful and appetising, the bar had a pleasant atmosphere, and the staff were always friendly and very helpful. Each evening the reception staff recommended and booked excellent reasonably priced restaurants away from the usual 'tourist traps' . The position of the hotel was ideal - just off Placa de Catalunya, so convenient for sightseeing buses or just for an interesting stroll around. La Rambla was 3 mins walk away. There was some traffic noise outside, but this was easily shut out by the windows, and efficient air conditioning in the room meant that there was no need to sleep with them open. All in all, a brilliant weekend break at The Pulitzer which we can recommend to you.
