<Author>mhcooper
<Content>Great Hotel 鈥?Couple of Quirky Things! Just came home from 2 weeks in Barcelona staying at 2 different hotels 鈥?both 4 star. The Hotel Pulitzer was by far the nicer hotel. I stayed there for 5 nights and had a wonderful stay. The hotel is rather modern and is located in a fantastic location. We walked the city North, South, East and West and the hotel could not have been a better starting place. If you take the subway you are 2 steps from a metro stop and the airport bus stops 2 steps away. There is also a Starbucks on the corner for those that need their coffee fix! We vacationed with friends so I can comment based on two different rooms.We were both on the 3rd floor. We were in the back and my friends in the front. As many Barcelona reviews indicate the street noise was obvious. If you are a light sleeper you might want to look for a hotel with a lot of floors and request a room high up! We had no trouble sleeping, but our friends were light sleepers. Also, the weather was unseasonably warm and the air-conditioning seems to only work in the summer. We opened up our window and were pretty comfortable.The look of the hotel is very modern and with all modern furniture you get a lot of deep cushions and it takes a while to get comfortable. The lobby and lobby bar has a lot of room to sit and relax or have a drink before and after dinner. We did not eat in the restaurant so I can not comment on the food.As for the quirky 鈥?the rooms are very comfortable 鈥?we had a queen size bed 鈥?but the room is long and narrow. On the wall at the foot of the bed is a flat screen TV that is easy to hit as you walk by it. Also, it may be a small thing, but there are no soap dishes in the bathroom so you never really know where to put the soap. Finally, the light switches are very hard to figure out. It took us 2 days just to figure out how to get the bed side table lights to stay on while the rest of the lights are turned off. In fact, our friend鈥檚 room there was some strange problem with the lighting controls as the left bed light was turned on by the switch on the right side while the right bed light was turned on by the switch when you walk in the door.All in all we loved out stay and would highly recommend the hotel 鈥?just be prepared to be surprised when you turn on the lights.

<Author>dawhitters
<Content>Loved it! We stayed at the Pulitzer in mid-December for one night on a EUR120 rate booked through the hotel's website.The hotel is nicely decorated, with well-designed rooms. Our room, on the street side of the hotel, was very quiet.. Be aware though, if you book a rate that is for a twin OR double room, your double will be two single beds pushed together, rather than a proper queen/king.The staff are very friendly - even the maids - and generally spoke English well. Front desk staff provided good restaurant recommendations with accompanying advice (e.g. don't eat paella at night - you won't sleep well).The location can't be beaten, right off Las Ramblas, but still in a relatively calm street.Only one thing really caused me concern. When we checked out, we asked a staff member to call us a taxi to the airport. He did this very efficiently, which was great. When the taxi turned up, the driver took our bags, put them in the trunk, and then went to talk to the staff member who had called him. This seemed a bit strange, since the driver already knew we were going to the airport. It looked to us as though the driver gave the staff member money, although it was done discretely.When we got to the airport, about EUR8 of extra charges were added to the meter (the charge normally used for tolls, etc). Not speaking Spanish well, I didn't want to argue, but something weird was going on. In total, the rate was about EUR10 more than going that other direction. I can't help but wonder if the driver pays that staff member to call him, and then passes the cost onto the guests.

<Content>Lovely design, excellent location, but not soundproof Hi,We stayed at this hotel on Jan 8 and 9, 2007. I booked this hotel via the hotel website, which is www.hotelpulitzer.es (or www.epoquehotels.com) and got a very good rate: 鈧?125 for a twin room including breakfast, excluding taxes (7%).We highly appreciated:- the excellent location (just off Plaza Catalu帽a): near bus stops for Aerobus, Bus Turistic, metro/train Catalunya. In the middle of the shopping area (Exaimple / Portal del Angel), and close to all tourist attractions.- the exquisite service: high level of service in the hotel. They are really friendly and helpfull, both in reception area, as in bar and restaurant.- the design: very stylish hotel. Are areas are very trendy and nicely decorated.- the hotel size: small hotel, so more personal service, no crowded public areas, no buffet queuing at breakfastWhat we disliked:- Rooms: although the rooms were very nice and the space was well occupied (rooms are rather small - deep, but narrow), you have all amenities: flat screen, domotica for the lighting, minibar, bathrobes, safe, desk with wifi/asdl, a lot of toiletries in the bathroom. BUT, now the down-side: the beds are rather small and uncomfortable and the walls are paper thin, so you here everything from nextdoors. Nevertheless, there was enough choice.Enjoy your stay at the Pulitzer!

<Content>Great Hotel My husband and I stayed 3 nights at the Hotel Pulitzer in December 2006. So if you stay here and you are a light sleeper ask for a back room!All in all though a great place to stay.

<Author>dafos27
<Content>Centrally Located We originally booked this hotel via Clarion Hotels, but the hotel was sold before we made the trip. The new owners honored our rate without fail. The Hotel Pulitzer is on a side street off Placa Catalunya. The hotel is very clean in the lobby, restaurant, bar, and in the rooms. Although the rooms are small, they are very comfortable. There was a huge closet to store your luggage, many shelves and drawers. You can pack all your clothes away if you're here for a week or more. The bathroom was equally large with a nice large granite sink and the shower has sliding glass door. The door to the bathroom does not open on a hinge, but slides on tracks, which was not obvious (initially). Toiletries are provided such as shampoo/conditioner, shower gel, razor w/cream, hand lotion, comb, toothbrush, robes, disposable flipflops, shoe shiners, and cotton pads for makeup. Way more necessities than most hotels provide. We had a balcony with two door french doors that looked down into the street. The A/C and heat worked fine and the rooms have a safe and LCD television. The room we had was on the second floor, close to the street so the noise level was louder than normal for most hotels. In Barcelona, trash is picked up at all hours of the night, but with the doors shut and the A/C on, it was not an issue for us. If you require complete quiet, you should not get a room on the street side or near the bar area. The hotel staff was very helpful with side trip arrangements and getting our taxis. I can't say enough good things about this hotel. The internet is available next door at the Hotel Regina for free. There are only two connections, so you might have to wait. The terrace on the top of the hotel was not open due to construction, but we did spend some time up there enjoying some views, but moreso the weather. Lastly, the hotel is centrally located to where all the action is. We walked to all the restaurants we ate at and it is a two minute walk to the Catalunya Metro stop which is one of the hubs of the metro system. Also, very close to Las Ramblas which is one of the main streets in Barcelona. You can't possibly go wrong with this hotel. Hope all this helps in your travels.  
<Date>Nov 29, 2006

<Author>rob10
<Content>Great Hotel, Central location My wife and I stayed here for 4 nights in September. It's a great hotel, right in the centre of Barcelona - ideal for visiting all the sights. It is also about 200m from the main airport bus stop, so is really easy to get to and from the airport, without carrying your bags very far.The hotel is very modern and the rooms are very tasteful - as everyone says, they are on the small side (but not tiny). Given this is a city break type place, you don't spend ages sat in your room.The hotel has a central atrium with the bar at the bottom. Some rooms on all floors come off this atrium. As there are no carpets, you can hear a bit of noise from the bar in these rooms. If you like a quieter room, I would specify this as a booking request.Otherwise the hotel is great, staff friendly etc, we would go back again.

<Author>Christi_R
<Content>Fabulous Hotel! I stayed at the Pulitzer Hotel for around a week at the end of August 06. I am from the US and in my mid 20s. The hotel was in a great location, just steps from the Placa Catalyuna and Las Ramblas and right near the metro stop. Since it is on a side street, the hotel was quiet. It is a perfect spot if you want to be right near the action, but not in the middle of it. It is walking distance from shopping in the Barrio Gotico and restaurants on the Paseig de Gracia. The hotel staff was very friendly, helpful, and spoke English. They even helped us map out a road trip. The room was a good size, the bed was a comfortable queen (which is hard to find), and the bathroom was modern and a good size. The hotel itself is modern, and has the feel of a luxury hotel with the personality and service of a small hotel. I would recommend this hotel to anyone going to Barcelona. I reserved the room through Clarion's website, and got a good rate. My only complaint about Clarion is if you book early and then need to cancel a day at the start of your trip, they will reprice your entire reservation. So if you book early, but may need to cancel a day, book two reservations on their website. We stayed at another hotel during our two week stay because the hotel was booked a few days, and all and all this was our favorite. The only thing missing was a business center with internet. However, I believe they have wireless if you bring your laptop. Barcelona is a great city, and the Pulitzer was top notch! I would like to go back.

<Author>npm123
<Content>Excellent stylish  Unlike most city centre hotels the Pulitzer is great value for money with friendly and helpful staff and clean comfortable rooms. As said in previous reviews the rooms are on the small side but well designed and perfect for a city stay.The lounge/bar area is has a nice atmosphere and the cocktails are excellent but the bar does close at 12pm.We had breakfast included in our package and this is well worth doing as it costs 15euros per person otherwise, although the breakfast selection is good.We ate one evening in the hotel as my wife was not well. The staff went out of their way to organise a plain pasta dish just for her when they realised she was not well.( not difficult to create but it was the thought we were impressed with). The food in the restaurant for dinner was good but is not cheap compared to other restaurants in the city.One thing to be aware off is parking. We had a hire car, having driven up the coast ,and the hotel parking is in the underground public car park next to the hotel. This cost was 25 euros per day and this was a discounted rate for the hotel !!Overall we were impressed with the standard and would definitely use the hotel again.

<Author>Jillette
<Content>Okay if you like late 1990's minimalism style design My review of the Pulitzer is probably biased by the fact that I spent the 3 nights before my stay there at the Hotel Colon, which has in my opinion the best location in central Barcelona. Yes, the Pulitzer is a triumph of design, but the location, on one of the dull streets off Catalunya is seedy at best, and the hotel lets itself down in a number of aspects. First point to note is that if you have vertigo, or just a pretty severe fear of heights, then this is NOT the hotel for you. The glass lifts had me quaking in my boots, and the waist high glass railings which look out over the ground floor bar on each floor were enough to make me feel ill. I also wondered at the sense of the waist high railings - very little to prevent the intoxicated leaping over. The rooftop terrace is nice, again once you don't have a fear of heights, however the bar never seemed to be open although the hotel literature said that it opened from 8pm. The rooms are fashionable and comfortable, although the overall black and white aesthetic gives a rather clinical lasting impression. The bathroom was also a good size, with plenty of toiletries, but the sink and shower really lets the hotel down. The sink, of a freestanding marble square style WOULD NOT DRAIN! If for example, you washed your teeth, the sink would fill up and then take twenty minutes to drain. This problem must have existed before our stay, so I'm very surprised that the hotel placed anyone in the room. The showerhead also could not be removed, which reminded me of public swimming baths. But, for those for whom alcohol is key, the bar on the ground floor is lovely (though smoking), and the strawberry daiquiris will take some beating.

<Author>blueaugusto
<Content>hard to fault and the glass lift is fantastic! I chose this hotel partly because I loved its funky decor from the website pictures, and I wasn't disappointed. The staff were friendly and courteous, though the barstaff were not too good on cocktails! Food in the restaurant was excellent, though sadly it's not open on sundays, meaning we had to resort to a limited and unimpressive room service menu. Rooms are small but tasteful with great bathrooms and showers, and I was sorely tempted to steal the wardrobe door handles as they were just what I'm looking for!The hotel has all the amenities you want - room safes, tv, great bar area, nice breakfast, newspapers, access to holmes gym with pool around the corner. I especially liked the glass lift (not so good if you're scared of heights!) and the way the rooms line the lobby which goes up to the roof - this means you can lean down from the 6th floor and shout at people in the bar!My only gripes would be the usual - not enough coat hangers (are hotels only allowed to have so many coat hangers on the premises?), no iron, crap room service menu and limited mini bar. Also the damn italian football supporters who sang and cheered all sunday nights whilst we were trying to sleep!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Hotel - bad soundproofing! Stayed here late March 2006. I agree with other reviews that this hotel is in an excellent location and that it is stylish. What has not been mentioned, and maybe it only affects rooms overlooking Bergara (or Vergara) Street, is the noise. We were on the first floor. The soundproofing on the balcony doors is non existant. The street and traffic noise from people going by lasts until about 4am. Then building work appeared to start close by, at least that is what it sounded like - rubble being poured down a funnel into a skip. The hotel next door looked like it was being renovated. Then there was the garbage collection. Then the street cleaners hose down the roads and pavements, then the morning traffic starts up again (except Sunday). Got about 4 hours sleep a night at best!Probably can't blame the hotel for the noise but they should put in better glazing.Other than that the hotel was great. Breakfast was filling and was a good start to the long day. The bar was relaxed and the roof terrace was nice for a rest and a view during the day or night, although the outdoor bar was not open when we were there (bring your own beer!). The Metro station is just round the corner and the bus from the Airport ( a bargain at 3.75 Euro) drops you off at the other side of Placa Catalunya Sq (outside the Cort Ingles department store). We will definitely return to Barcelona, and now that we know where everything is, will have a more relaxing time.  
<Date>Apr 5, 2006

<Author>Minky007
<Content>Lovely hotel We stayed at the hotel for two nights, for a wedding anniversary trip to Barcelona.The hotel is on a side road. It is in a fantastic location, just off Placa Catalunya. Make sure you take the open top bus from here. This is the best way to see the city and gain perspective.We arrived before our room was ready (at 1pm) but they quickly sorted this. Our room (111) was lovely. Long and narrow but didn't feel small (probably because of the high ceilings). The bathroom was also lovely with big fluffy towels!Within a few minutes of being in our room, there was a knock on the door and a bottle of Champagne, with the compliments of the hotel staff (for our anniversary). A lovely little touch!I only have a couple of negative comments for the hotel. First, the English language TV channels in the room are limited. We didn't spend very much time in the room but it would've been nice to watch something other than Sky News/CNN/MTV when we were there!Second, is that the hotel is noisy. This is due to a combination of hardwood floors throughout the hotel and open internal balconies on each floor, which made noise travel and echo throughout the building.My tip for this is to request a room as far away from the lifts as possible. I can't guarantee that this will solve the problem but may help!Barcelona is a fantastic city. Lots to see and do and great food.If you don't mind paying, go to Noti and Moo for some delicious food!!

<Author>timdon
<Content>Excellent apart from a sore shoulder Pulitzer is in possibly the best location in Barcelona - just off the Parc de Catalunya, one minute from the top of Las Ramblas. Inside, the hotel looks great and the staff are extremely helpful. The rooms are on the smaller side, but not uncomfortably so and we were asked on arrival if we wanted a queen bed rather than two singles so no complaints there. The bathroom was good with both power shower and bath. The bar is a great place to relax and there is a health club with pool about 5 minutes away. Whilst Pulitzer has all the ingredients of an excellent hotel, unfortunately it's not quite there. The rooms look great but the finish in ours (211) was poor in places: many of the metal switch and socket covers were loose, I had to fix a bedside light and the air con wasn't particularly powerful. However possibly the worst design glitch was hanging the plasma TV five feet up a wall only a foot and a half from the end of the bed - this meant anyone over four and a half foot tall (i.e. me) caught their shoulder on it everytime they walked by). Despite these minor glitches, this is still a very good hotel in a superb location and I would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent base to explore Barcelona I surprised my wife with a trip to Barcelona for her birthday and after a shaky start (missed connecting flight in Frankfurt) we arrived at The Pulitzer, late, tired and stressed. First impression was that it is much bigger than it appears on the websites. Once inside it is as funky and contemporary as I had expected. The staff made us feel very welcome and give us a good room with a balcony. OK the rooms aren鈥檛 huge but they aren鈥檛 pokey either. We found our room very comfortable and relaxing. As for street noise or banging doors, we hardly noticed it. The hotel bar is great for just hanging/chilling out after a hard day shopping and its also worth checking out the roof terrace, weather permitting. Breakfast was a little expensive I thought and yes the scrambled eggs are smelly but they taste fine. On the whole this is a contemporary, relaxed hotel with a brilliant location (easy walking distance for great food, shopping and sight seeing) and great staff in a great city and I would stay here again, no problem. Lastly if you鈥檙e lucky enough to have Ed on reception he is a diamond for recommending great places to eat and pointing you in the right direction. D.

<Author>SCJL
<Content>Hip but quirky My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Pulitzer for 4 nights recently. The hotel is really new and hip and has a great restaurant. It is also in a great location near the Rambla, within walking distance to many tourist sites in the city. On the other hand, the place has its quirks that get old pretty quickly. Our room had recurring electrical and heat problems and while the staff was friendly, they were pretty ineffectual about really fixing anything or making any reasonable accommodation on our rates, etc. Also, while the hardwood floors are really nice appearance-wise, they also result in a pretty considerable amount of noise being transmitted from room to room. In all a good hotel for the money, but it still seems to have some growing pains to work out.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Convenient and Contemporary We paid US $200 + tax for this room and felt that was a bit much for what we got. HOWEVER, if you are looking for a modern hotel with the perfect location, and are not willing to pay top dollar, then the Pulitzer is a good choice.There are a few drawbacks. The rooms are very small (we only bring carry-on luggage when we travel, yet there was barely room to store it). We also found that the maids had not cleaned our room very well when we arrived.On the plus side, the furnishings were stylish and new. The lobby and adjacent bar were sleek and inviting, with numerous cozy couches and a library of books. The breakfast (included in the price we paid) was much more than we expected, and offered a large assortment of fresh pastries, rolls, meats, and fruit.The location is the best feature, however. The hotel literally sits in the center of where you want to be. Walk one way and you get to the waterfront. Walk the other way and you're on the major shopping thoroughfare. Walk the other way and you hit some of the architectural highlights. Ironically, it is tucked away on a street that doesn't get much traffic, and is pretty quiet. For us, the perfect location is what makes the Pulitzer a place we'd return to.

<Author>Moreea1
<Content>A Must Stay! My daughter and I stayed in Spain for 7 days and ended up at the Pulitzer after our experience at the first hotel went bad. We randomly walked in and asked if they had rooms available and they were able to accomodate us for the remaining of our trip. After reading a few of the reviews about smelly eggs, no hot water, and small rooms. I'm sorry to say but it is Europe, learn to deal. I'm Spanish American and smelly eggs are farm fresh eggs which Americans are not use to eating (our chickens are raised on steroids). The rooms are not as small as people have stated. Yes, there is hot water! If you are like me that only likes 4 stars and above this is the place to stay. You are on the corner of the center near all the top shops and Las Ramblas. The staff is very friendly and helpful with anything you need. The hotel is located in a safe place of town where you can walk at any time of day or night. The breakfast is prepared Spanish style and very fresh and delicious. The rate is not bad at all considering the center location. If you are looking for a great, safe and nice place to stay I totally recommend this hotel.

<Author>SonOfBruin2
<Content>nice location, excellent service I stayed at the Hotel Pulitzer from August 15-19 with my family in two double rooms. The rooms are small (maybe 9 feet across), as noted by other reviewers, but they are well laid out and appointed nicely with modern furnishings and prints. One room (which we moved out of) had a support column in the middle, but most other rooms do not (I think it was room 314). There was minimal noise from outside the hotel, but any noise from the hall reverberates in your room, especially doors slamming. None of us really figured out the funky recessed lighting switches, but that was a non-issue really. My only other minor gripe was with the air conditioning (individual thermostats, but the hotel controls the a/c?), which all of Spain it seems has yet to master. The location could not have been much better -- literally within walking distance of everything. There is no gym on site but you get free access to the Holmes Place gym 4 blocks away. It doesn't compare to U.S. mega-gyms, but it's better than most hotel fitness rooms, and there is a pool, sauna, steam room, and towel service. At the hotel there is a lovely rooftop deck/garden for sunbathing during the day, and the bar hosts a weekly event there on Thursday nights -- very cool. The lobby is ultra-hip and boasts a large fragrant bouquet, a bar within the hotel's atrium, and a small library and reading room. It all feels very Design Within Reach.The service is the greatest asset of the Hotel Pulitzer. Every staff member is very friendly, helpful, and speaks English (maybe not the housekeeping staff). At the breakfast buffet (which I highly recommend) we complained that the scrambled eggs smelled/tasted weird and were politely offered fried eggs instead -- and they were delicious. The following mornings, upon entering the restaurant, the waitress remembered us and asked how many fried eggs we would like that morning -- THAT'S service. The tasty pastries are worth a mention as well. The front desk also recommended a tapas bar not far from the hotel -- Ciudad Condal -- which I in turn highly recommend to everyone else. When my camera broke and we tried to contact a Canon store in Barcelona, the woman at the front desk called for us to inquire about store location/hours. I cannot stress enough just how great all the staff were. I would stay here again (if I ever make it back to Barcelona).  
<Date>Aug 25, 2005

<Content>A nice Hotel with a great location, but..... My wife and I had two separate stays at the Hotel Clarion Pulitzer hotel in August this year, both stays was booked through Expedia, as separate bookings. I will start to say: The hotel is only one year old, and generally nice, except for a few thinks about the rooms. In the two different rooms we had, the material of the sink in the bathrooms was not of marble or of porcelain, but of a stone material. Unfortunately the stone material, after what I could understand, can not bee cleaned orderly with usual cleaning remedies, and the sinks therefore looked a bit unhygienic, with stains on it. The same problem was also with the stone tiles on the bathroom floors.The two rooms we had, was after my opinion, on the small side.I find it also strange that an only one year old hotel is not better soundproofed. There was a little noise from the corridor and from the street.The location of the hotel is very great and central, the staff in the reception is both polite and also helpful concerning giving advice about what to see, what to do and for example - how to use the public transportation system in Barcelona and the surroundings.The Hotel has a Bar and a Restaurant, but I could not observe many guests in the Restaurant.If you don't have breakfast included in your reservation, it could be wise to eat another place. Unfortunately, our second stay from 13th to 15th August 2005 was an unpleasant experience. However the Hotel promised us to sort out the reservation problem 鈥?while we were on a weeks cruise. After returning to the Hotel on Saturday 13th August, to our surprise the staff had not done anything to solve the problem. When I called Expedia on my mobile, after a few minutes I got contact with a very service-minded and professional employee from Expedia, which sorted out the reservation problem with the Hotel.If you should meet problems with your reservation at the Hotel Clarion Pulitzer Hotel, my advice is then to take immediate action on yourselves, and not only thrust what the hotel staff tells you.

<Content>Fantastic hotel, staff and value From a recommendation on this site, my husband, son and I spent a week at the Pulitzer this month. It's perfectly located on a quiet street right off the Plaza Catalunya, two blocks from the start of La Rambla (main walking street) and all roads leading to other parts of town. The hotel is brand new, not yet listed in all the guide books, boutique-style, modern and friendly. Lots of dark wood, white sofas/furniture, modern art and very high ceilings. The rooms are built around an atrium with glass elevators. The rooms are very large, clean, modern, quiet and have a flat screen tv and the bathrooms are very large with all the amenities.The spacious bar/lobby area is an oasis from the hot weather - the bartenders are spirited and friendly. You have a choice to sit outside or in a lovely garden for breakfast. The breakfast is included in the room rate and offers many choices from all kinds of fruit to eggs, meats, cheeses, breads, cereals and yogurt.The front desk staff is fantastic. Everyone speaks English and are all knowledgeble and friendly. Julian, the night manager, knows all the ins and outs of Barcelona from years of experience in the hotel business in Barcelona.I highly recommend this hotel and will return; we had a great trip to Barcelona!

<Author>Massimo_C
<Content>Don't pay top dollar... This hotel enjoys a perfect location. It's on a side street between the start of La Rambla (main walking street) and roads leading to the nicer, less touristy end of town. There are a few other hotels next door and across the road (Best Western Regina  Catalonia). Style:Boutique, modern and cooly casual. Lots of dark wood and white sofas/furniture. The photos depict the style accurately, but the quality is not exceptional. The hotel tries to be fashionable looking and a little arty. Room style was modern and had flat screen tv. Highpoints:Room size - quite good. Our room had a balcony overlooking the street - not much to see, but nice regardless. Bathroom generally well sized, with modern fixtures. Very clean.Bar area was relaxed and spacious - big, white leather lounges, red asian looking bar etc. The breakfast area was lovely - with bright, airy inside seating and a pretty courtyard outside with flowers and sunshine. Helpful concierge, no attitude.Lowpoints:The hotel claims 4 stars, however nothing was done to make our stay special. No turn down service, no flowers etc. We were given two separately made single beds which had been pushed together, which I thought unusual. No bath, no tea/coffee making facilities, only 1 english tv station (CNN), no iron. The shower itself wasn't lit and was black, so a little dark.Breakfast was average, apart from the setting. In my view, the quality of a hotel's scambled eggs is very important - here: inedible. There was a little noise from the street and from the hallway - ie rooms didn't appear well soundproofed.Not all the furnishings were high quality and in parts the hotel looked a little cheap in execution. Ie, don't expect polished, luxury furnishings and you won't be disappointed. Would I stay again:I have no real complaints and would not advise someone against staying here. No doubt you would be quite comfortable. But depending on the money, next time I'd consider somewhere else in the same area. Don't pay a fortune for it. Have stayed in far nicer places for the euros we paid here.  
<Date>Jun 5, 2005

<Content>We love the Pulitzer! My husband and I recently returned from a trip to Europe. While in Barcelona, we stayed at the Pulitzer for 6 nights and cannot rave enough about it. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A wonderful choice for Barca My husband and I stayed here for 4 nights in early April, and we would definitely return, no question. It's on a side street right next to Placa Catalunya, v. convenient to anywhere you want to go, and we were not bothered by street noise. The staff was excellent, quite friendly and helpful. I saw desk staff switch between english, spanish, catalan, and french without batting an eye, and they helped us make arrangements to the airport (cab ride was about 25EUR, 35 minutes on a weekday morning) and lent us an ethernet cable to use the broadband connx in the room. The pics on the hotel website are quite accurate. The desk, lobby, and bar are tasteful and modern, very comfortable. Glass elevators, and you can look down from all floors to see the bar area and check out what's going on. The roof terrace is nice too.Our room was on the small side at the end of a hall as we booked through expedia, but perfectly decorated, very sleek and modern w/ hardwood floors, marble bath, flat panel tv mounted on the wall, lots of dark wood. V. comfortable double bed, and windows opened. You control the thermostat, and the lights are all on dimmers. They provide robes, slippers, lots of towels, hair dryer, and other toiletries.We checked out the bar one night, and it's a fairly quiet but relaxing scene with lots of seating on couches. Great bartenders. The restaurant was nice too, we ate a delicious breakfast there each day, and they have everything you could possibly want.If you are a light sleeper, you might be disturbed by noise from other guests. The doors all have a tendancy to close heavily, and you can hear voices from the hall now and then. Nothing earplugs wouldn't take care of, and it didn't really bother us. We also didn't check out the health club next door, but were told we were entitled to free passes. Maybe next time.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel - really pleased with it. We stayed at the Pulitzer for 5 nights. It's a well designed minimalist style hotel. The rooms are very good - we stayed at the front and it's totally quiet with the windows closed. With them open ( we like the fresh air and it was fresh, believe me), it's still ok since it's not a very noisy street.It was a cold stay in Barcelona - it snowed for a few hours one day. But it was always a pleasure to come back to the Pulitzer - lovely and warm and staff always welcoming. The location is ideal for Catalunya Square with quick access to all transport, tourist buses, airport buses and La Rambla.The staff are really friendly, efficient and helpful. We didn't eat dinner at the hotel but the menu looked good. Breakfast was just right for us - buffet style but staff helping you in their usual efficient way.We like finding good hotels - it's always a pleasant surprise. This is a good one. We'd very happily go back - now if we could. And, it confirmed how useful Tripadvisor is. We had booked another hotel until we read their reviews ( yes, I know, I should have done that first ). We cancelled and found this via Tripadvisor.
